APPRAISAL OF
AGRICULTURE AND AGRO-INDUSTRIES II PROJECT
YUGOSLAVIA
Statement of Operations and Policies for the Project
and the Sub-Project Appraisal Criteria
1.        The IBT and the SBS would follow the following policies, procedures,
terms and conditions in appraising and granting the sub-loans.
2         Montenegrin Project.  Before receiving long-term loans the Agro-
kombinat would up-date the appraisal estimates and submit the loan applica-
tion to IBT. IBT would review the loan application to take account of pos-
sible changes in the economic and market environment and to evaluate the
financial viability of the subproject and satisfy itself of the continued
credit-worthiness of the Agrokombinat.
3.        Macedonian Project.  For long-term loans to social sector enter-
prises, SBS would appraise each sub-project to ensure that: (a) sub-projects
provide satisfactory financial and economic rates of return on the basis
of detailed and realistic estimates of costs and benefits, and would generate
sufficient cash flow to cover debt service, legal claims, compulsory alloca-
tions to the enterprise's funds and reinvestment needs. Special justification
will be required if the financial rate of return is below 12%; (b) sub-projects
are technically feasible based on a critical review of technical data and
specifications provided by the sub-borrowers; (c) the market facilities for
the incremental production are available, and the supply of raw materials
is assured; (d) the sub-borrowers are credit-worthy, have the necessary
managerial competence to implement the sub-project and maintain a satisfactory
financial structure. As a guideline, the long-term financial structure, debt/
equity ratio should not exceed 3:1. Exceptions may be allowed (based on the
financial and economic merit of the sub-project) provided that the enterprise
enters into an agreement with a bank to increase its equity over a suitable
period of time to not less than 25% of its total capitalization; (e) adequate
physical and price "contingency" allowances are made. The "contingency"
allowance should take into account, inter alia, escalation clauses which may
be included in contracts. The appraisal report for each sub-project should
indicate the date to which base cost estimates refer and should discuss the
"contingency" allowances made; (f) appropriate consideration is given and
explicitly recorded in the appraisal report to the need for introduction of
capital-intensive automated technology as opposed to more labor-intensive
methods and to the consequences of such a choice on the investment and operat-
ing costs of the sub-projects.



ANNEX 12
Page 2
4.        Sub-projects in the private sector in Macedonia would normally be
submitted to the SBS by social sector enterprises which, having aggregated
investment proposals of several private farmers, would borrow on their behalf.
However, private farmers may also submit directly investment proposals to
SBS. In appraising sub-projects in the private sector, the SBS would satisfy
itself that:
(a) sub-projects are technically feasible, financially viable,
commercially sound and economically justified, and markets
and processing facilities for their incremental production
are available;
(b) sub-projects would generate sufficient cash flow to cover
debt service, legal claims and needs for reinvestment;
(c) adequate and continuing technical asistance, and suitable
market outlets at fair and reasonable prices are available to
the private farmers;
(d) in the case of lending through social sector organizations,
the cooperation agreements are adequate.
Financing Plan for Sub-projects
5.        The sub-borrowers wou:Ld provide a minimum of 20% of investment
costs. The banks would provide loans up to 80% of the sub-projects costs.
The Bank funds would finance 100% of the estimated foreign exchange part of
the project cost. Prior to disbursing the Bank loan the banks would assure
the availability of their own ftnds and sub-borrowers' contribution for each
specific sub-project.
Repayment Period of Sub-loans
6.        The term of sub-loans would be determined in  accordance with the
cash-flow projections of the investments, after careful estimates of the re-
payment capacity of the sub-borrower have been made. However, the grace and
repayment period on IBRD funds will not exceed the following:
Maximum Grace Period   Maximum Total Term
Years
Macedonia
Social Sector                             3                        14
Private Sector                            5                        10
Montenegro                                3                        15
